Contradiction in Absolute Existence as the Necessary
Contradiction between claim and philosophers' own statements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that the Necessary is absolute existence contradicts the philosophers' own definitions of absolute existence as a mental predicate and secondary intelligible.

Core Idea
Absolute existence cannot be the Necessary because it depends on a subject and is a mere mental accident.

The philosophers sometimes identify the Necessary Being with 'absolute existence', but this contradicts their own technical vocabulary. In this passage, the author points out two explicit statements from them that show absolute existence is a mind-dependent predicate and a secondary intelligible — both of which preclude it from being the self-subsistent foundation of reality. Let's examine how the author uses their own words against them.

Guided Path
1
Understand the argument's structure
The passage presents a contradiction: if the Necessary is absolute existence, then it conflicts with two of the philosophers' own claims. We'll read each claim and see why it creates a problem.
2
First contradiction: mental predicate
Read the definition of 'mental predicate' carefully. Notice that such predicates cannot exist independently of a subject. Compare to the Necessary, which is completely independent.
3
Second contradiction: secondary intelligible
Understand what a secondary intelligible is: an accident that attaches to a primary concept and has no external counterpart. If absolute existence is such, it cannot be the ultimate reality.
4
Reflect on the strategic value
Ask yourself: why is it effective for the author to use the philosophers' own terms against them? How does this strengthen the refutation?
This shows internal inconsistency, not just an external critique.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم القول بكون الواجب هو الوجود المطلق ينافي تصريحهم بأمور منها : أن الوجود المطلق من المحمولات العقلية، أي الأمور التي يمتنع استغناؤها عن المحل عقلاً ويمتنع حصولها فيـه بحسب الخارج كالإمكان والماهية بخلاف مثل الإنسان فإنه مستغن عن المحل، ومثل البياض فإن قيامه بالمحل خارجي ومنها أنه من المعقولات الثانية أي العوارض التي تلحق المعقولات الأولى من حيث لا يحاذي بها أمر
Then the claim that the Necessary is absolute existence contradicts their explicit statements in several matters. Among them is that absolute existence is among the mental predicates (al-maḥmūlāt al-'aqliyya), i.e., matters whose independence from a subject is impossible intellectually and whose occurrence in it externally is impossible, like possibility and quiddity, contrary to something like 'man' which is independent of a subject, and like whiteness whose subsistence in a subject is external. And among them is that it is among the secondary intelligibles, i.e., the accidents that attach to primary intelligibles insofar as they do not correspond to anything.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage presents an argument from contradiction. The author states that the claim that the Necessary is absolute existence directly contradicts the philosophers' own explicit statements (taṣrīḥihim). Two contradictions are cited: (1) Absolute existence is among the 'mental predicates' (al-maḥmūlāt al-'aqliyya). These are attributes that cannot exist independently of a subject (mahall) in the mind and cannot occur externally. Examples include possibility (imkan) and quiddity (mahiyya). In contrast, concepts like 'man' are independent of a subject, and whiteness (bayad) has external subsistence in a subject. If absolute existence is such a predicate, it requires a subject for its subsistence, whereas the Necessary is self-subsistent. (2) Absolute existence is among the 'secondary intelligibles' (al-ma'qulat al-thaniyya), which are mental accidents that attach to primary intelligibles and do not correspond to any external reality. Thus, it cannot be the Necessary Being, which is the foundation of all reality. This shows an internal inconsistency in the philosophers' position if they claim the Necessary is absolute existence.

محل

ماهية

معقولات ثانية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that because 'absolute existence' sounds universal and all-encompassing, it must be the highest reality (the Necessary).
Correction: The philosophers' own definitions show absolute existence is a mental construction dependent on a subject and lacking external reality, so it cannot be the Necessary.

Checkpoint
Why does absolute existence being a 'mental predicate' contradict its being the Necessary?
A) Because mental predicates have external existence
B) Because mental predicates require a subject and the Necessary is self-subsistent
C) Because the Necessary is also a mental predicate
D) Because mental predicates are external

Key Takeaway
The philosophers' own admission that absolute existence is a mental predicate and secondary intelligible shows it cannot be the self-subsistent Necessary Being.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you claim something about Allah, do you check whether that claim contradicts other things you already hold true about Him? When was the last time you realized a belief you held was internally inconsistent, and what did you do about it?
?
The philosophers here built a whole system on 'absolute existence' as the Necessary, but their own definitions exposed the flaw. Are there any ideas you hold about Allah that you have never critically examined, because they 'sound philosophical' or 'complex'? Will you now go back and check them against the clear teachings of the Qur'an and Sunnah?
?
This passage warns that a concept like 'absolute existence' is a mental accident, not a real being—yet we can easily fall into treating abstract intellectual constructs as if they are real. Can you identify any abstract concept (like 'destiny', 'love of Allah', 'tawakkul') that you have turned into a mental category rather than a living reality? What would it take to move from intellectual abstraction to heartfelt submission?

Existence Has No Genus or Species: Argument and Refutation
The author argues that existence is simple and refutes the inference to the Necessary Being.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that existence is simple and has no genus or species, and why it does not prove existence is the Necessary Being.

Core Idea
Existence's simplicity does not entail it is the Necessary Being.

This passage presents a key theological argument about the nature of existence. Some thinkers claimed that because existence is simple (has no parts), it must be the Necessary Being. The author first outlines this argument and then critically examines its logical weaknesses. Let's follow the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the claim
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Identify the central claim: existence has no genus or differentia.
The claim is stated in the first sentence: 'الوجود ليس له جنس ولا فصل'.
2
Understand the argument for simplicity
The argument proceeds by reductio: if existence had parts (genus/differentia), then the part would precede the whole, leading to self-priority or priority over its opposite. Follow each of the three sub-arguments.
There are two cases: if the part is existence, then self-priority; if non-existence, then priority of thing over its opposite.
3
Note the generality argument
The opponents also argue that genus must be more general than the species, but nothing is more general than existence, so existence cannot have a genus.
4
Examine the author's critique
The author points out that some premises are weak. Even if all premises are accepted, the argument does not prove that existence is the Necessary Being because it uses two affirmative premises in the second figure, which yields no conclusion.
The author stresses the need to establish equivalence (مساواة) between the attributes of existence and the Necessary Being.
5
Reflect on the logical flaw
Consider why a second-figure syllogism with two affirmatives fails. The author's point is that shared attributes do not imply identity unless equivalence is proven.
This is a key lesson in logical reasoning within kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها قولهم : الوجود ليس له جنس ولا فصل، لأنه بسيط لا جزء له عيناً ولا ذهناً، وإلا لزم تقدمه على نفسه ضرورة تقدم وجود الجزء على وجود الكل في الخارج، إن كان التركب خارجياً، وفي الذهن إن كان ذهنياً، ولأن جزءه وإن كان وجوداً موجوداً لزم تقدم الشيء على نفسه، وإن كان عدماً أو معدوماً لزم تقدم الشيء بنقيضه، ولأن الجنس يجب أن يكون أعم ولا أعم من الوجود إذ ما من شيء إلا وله وجود، وفي بعض المقدمات ضعف لا يخفى، ولو سلم فغاية الأمر اتصاف كل من الوجود الواجب بهذه المعاني، ولا إنتاج عن الموجبتين في الشكل الثاني . وتحقيقه أن لزوم هذه الأمور للوجود لا يوجب كونه الواجب ما لم تتبين مساواتها للملزوم.
Among their statements: existence has no genus and no differentia, because it is simple, having no part externally nor mentally; otherwise it would necessitate its own priority, necessarily the priority of the existence of the part over the existence of the whole in the external if the composition is external, and in the mind if mental; and because if its part is an existing existence, it would necessitate the priority of the thing over itself, and if it is non-existence or non-existent, it would necessitate the priority of the thing over its opposite; and because the genus must be more general, and nothing is more general than existence, for there is nothing except that it has existence, and some premises have an obvious weakness; and if it is granted, the utmost is the attribution of each—existence and the Necessary Being—with these meanings, and no conclusion is produced from two affirmatives in the second figure. The verification is that the entailment of these things for existence does not necessitate it being the Necessary Being unless their equivalence to the entailing thing is clarified.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes an argument that attributes of existence (lack of genus and differentia) show it must be the Necessary Being. The author first states the opponents' claim: existence has no genus (جنس) or differentia (فصل) because it is simple (بسيط), having no parts. Then he notes the necessary consequence: if it had parts, the part's existence would precede the whole, entailing self-priority. Also, if the part were existent, that would be self-priority; if non-existent, then the thing would be prior to its opposite. Further, genus must be more general, but nothing is more general than existence. The author then notes that some of these premises are weak. Even if granted, the most that follows is that both existence and the Necessary Being have these attributes, which yields no conclusion in the second figure of syllogism (two affirmative premises). The key point: the attributes of existence do not prove it is the Necessary Being unless equivalence (مساواة) between the two is established.

Key Terms
جنس
فصل
بسيط
تقدم
وجود
واجب
شكل ثاني
مساواة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that because existence is simple and cannot have a genus, it must be the Necessary Being.
Correction: The author shows this inference is invalid without proof of equivalence between the attributes of existence and the Necessary Being.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say that even if existence has no genus or differentia, it does not prove it is the Necessary Being?
A) Because existence is a mental concept, not real
B) Because no conclusion follows from two affirmative premises in the second figure without establishing equivalence
C) Because existence is an accident, not a substance
D) Because the Necessary Being is not existence

Key Takeaway
The attributes of existence do not automatically prove it is the Necessary Being without establishing equivalence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The author warns against concluding that two things are identical just because they share some attributes. In your life, have you ever mistaken a superficial similarity for an essential truth? How can you ensure your judgments are based on more than surface-level comparisons?
?
This lesson shows that even a flawed argument can be granted for the sake of discussion, but the truth still stands. Are there areas of your faith where you feel pressure to produce perfect arguments? Could you instead rest in the certainty that God has given you, even when human reasoning seems incomplete?

Five Reasons Absolute Existence Cannot Be the Necessary Being
Enumeration of five reasons against identifying absolute existence with the Necessary Being.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five rational arguments demonstrating that absolute existence (الوجود المطلق) is incompatible with the attributes of the Necessary Being (الواجب).

Core Idea
Absolute existence is a mental abstraction, not a self-subsistent divine reality.

In this passage, the author systematically refutes the claim that the Necessary Being is identical to absolute existence. He presents five distinct reasons showing that absolute existence possesses properties—such as being a mental predicate, divisible, multiply instantiated, and analogically predicated—that cannot apply to the unique, necessary, and indivisible Creator. Each reason builds a case that identifying the Necessary Being with absolute existence leads to contradictions.

Guided Path
1
Read the whole passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get a sense of the argument flow. Notice how the author lists reasons with 'منها' (among them).
There are five clear reasons; try to spot them before reading the commentary.
2
Examine reasons 1 and 2 on mental status
Reasons 1 and 2 argue that absolute existence belongs to mental predicates and secondary intelligibles—meaning it cannot exist independently outside the mind. Understand why this disqualifies it from being the Necessary Being.
Compare with examples like 'man' (independent) and 'whiteness' (inheres externally).
3
Analyze reasons 3, 4, and 5 on divisibility and predication
Reasons 3–5 show that absolute existence is divisible into necessary/possible, multiplies by subjects, and is predicated by analogy—all impossible for the One Necessary Being.
Consider how 'multiplication by subjects' challenges the uniqueness of the Necessary Being.
4
Study the objection and response
The author raises an objection that the subject is independent of existence, then answers by clarifying the logical subject and intellectual inherence.
This nuance shows the depth of the Kalam discussion on predication.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that the view rests on corrupt principles and contradicts rational consensus. Summarize in your own words why absolute existence cannot be God.
The final sentence lists the corrupt principles: unity in person, external existence, impossibility of non-existence, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم القول بكون الواجب هو الوجود المطلق ينافي تصريحهم بأمور منها : أن الوجود المطلق من المحمولات العقلية، أي الأمور التي يمتنع استغناؤها عن المحل عقلاً ويمتنع حصولها فيه بحسب الخارج كالإمكان والماهية بخلاف مثل الإنسان فإنه مستغن عن المحل، ومثل البياض فإن قيامه بالمحل خارجي ومنها أنه من المعقولات الثانية أي العوارض التي تلحق المعقولات الأولى من حيث لا يحاذي بها أمر في الخارج، كالكلية والجزئية والذاتية والعرضية، لأنها أمور تلحق حقائق الأشياء عند حصولها في العقل وليس في الأعيان شيء هو الوجود أو الذاتية أو العرضية مثلاً. وإنما في الأعيان الإنسان والسواد مثلاً وههنا نظر من جهة أن ما انساق إليه البيان هو أن وجودات الأشياء من المحمولات العقلية والمعقولات الثانية وكان الكلام في الوجود المطلق، ومنها أنه ينقسم إلى الواجب والممكن، لأنه إن كان مفتقراً إلى سبب فممكن وإلا فواجب وإلى القديم والحادث، لأنه إن كان مسبوقاً بالغير أو بالعدم فحادث وإلا فقدم، ومنها أنه يتكثر بتكثر الموضوعات الشخصية كوجود زيد وعمرو والنوعية كوجود الإنسان والفرس، والجنسية كوجود الحيوان والنبات . فإن قيل : الموضوع هو المحل المستغني في قوامه عن ذلك الوجود ولا يتصور الحال، قلنا : المراد ههنا ما يقابل المحمول وهو الذي يحمل عليه الوجود بالاشتقاق، ولو سلم فالقيام ههنا عقلي، والماهية تلاحظ دون الوجود، وهذا معنى استغنائه عن العارض، وإن كان لا ينفك عن وجود عقلي، وظاهر هذا الكلام أن وجودات الممكنات إنما هي نفس الوجود المطلق، تكثرت بالإضافة إلى المحل، وليست أموراً متكثرة متخصصة بأنفسها معروضة له، وكان المراد أن الوجود المطلق يتكثر ما صدق هو عليه من الوجودات الخاصة بتكثر الموضوعات ومنها أنه مقول على الوجودات بالتشكيك، كما سبق. وجميع ذلك مما يستحيل في حق الواجب تعالى وتقدس. وبالجملة فالقول بكون الواجب هو الوجود المطلق مبني على أصول فاسدة، مثل كونه واحداً بالشخصي موجوداً في الخارج ممتنع العدم لذاته ومستلزم لبطلان أمور اتفق العقلاء عليها، مثل كونه أعرف الأشياء مشتركاً بين الوجودات مقولاً عليها بالتشكيك
Then the claim that the Necessary Being is absolute existence contradicts their explicit statements in matters, among them: (1) that absolute existence is among mental predicates, i.e., things whose independence from a subject is impossible intellectually and whose occurrence in it is impossible externally, like possibility and quiddity—unlike, for example, man, for he is independent of a subject, and like whiteness, for its inherence in a subject is external. (2) And among them that it is among secondary intelligibles, i.e., the accidents that attach to primary intelligibles insofar as they do not correspond to any external thing, like universality, particularity, essentiality, and accidentally—because they are things that attach to the realities of things when they occur in the mind, and there is nothing in concrete reality that is, for example, existence or essentiality or accidentally; rather, in concrete reality there is, for example, man and blackness. And there is a point of view here: that what the exposition leads to is that existences of things are among mental predicates and secondary intelligibles, but the discussion was about absolute existence. (3) And among them that it divides into necessary and possible, because if it is in need of a cause, it is possible, otherwise necessary; and into eternal and originated, because if it is preceded by another or by non-existence, it is originated, otherwise eternal. (4) And among them that it multiplies by the multiplicity of personal subjects, like the existence of Zayd and Amr; and by specific, like the existence of man and horse; and by generic, like the existence of animal and plant. Then it is said: The subject is the substrate independent in its essence from that existence, and the inherence is not conceivable. We say: What is meant here is what stands over against the predicate, that upon which existence is predicated by derivation; and if it is granted, the inherence here is intellectual, and quiddity is considered without existence, and this is the meaning of its independence from the accident, even if it is not free from a mental existence. And apparent from this speech is that existences of possibles are nothing but absolute existence itself, multiplied by relation to the subject, and they are not many things particularized in themselves that act as subjects for it; and the meaning was that absolute existence multiplies, in terms of what it is true of—the particular existences—by the multiplicity of subjects. (5) And among them that it is predicated of existences by analogy, as previously. All of this is impossible with respect to the Necessary Being, exalted and sanctified. In summary, the claim that the Necessary Being is absolute existence is built upon corrupt principles, such as it being one in person, existent externally, impossible of non-existence by itself, and entails the nullification of matters upon which the rational people agree, such as it being the most known of things, shared among existences, predicated of them by analogy.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage enumerates five reasons why identifying the Necessary Being (الواجب) with absolute existence (الوجود المطلق) is contradictory. The author first states that absolute existence belongs to 'mental predicates' (المحمولات العقلية), which cannot exist independently of a subject in the external world—like possibility or quiddity—unlike concrete entities like man or whiteness that inhere externally. Second, it belongs to 'secondary intelligibles' (المعقولات الثانية), which are mental accidents attaching to primary concepts (e.g., universality) and have no external counterpart; thus absolute existence is a mental concept, not a concrete reality. Third, absolute existence is divisible into necessary and possible, eternal and originated—but the Necessary Being is indivisible. Fourth, it multiplies by the multiplicity of subjects (personal, specific, generic), whereas the Necessary Being is absolutely one. An objection is raised: the 'subject' (المحل) is independent of existence, so inherence is inconceivable. The author answers that by 'subject' here is meant the logical subject on which existence is predicated, and the inherence is intellectual; quiddity is considered without existence, meaning it is independent of the accidental mental existence, though not without a mental existence. This implies that particular existences are just absolute existence multiplied by relation to subjects. Fifth, absolute existence is predicated of its instances by analogy (تشكيك), implying gradation, which is incompatible with the Necessary Being's unicity. All these properties are impossible for the Necessary Being. The conclusion: the view that the Necessary Being is absolute existence rests on corrupt principles, such as it being one in person, externally existent, necessarily existent by itself, and entails denying universal agreements like it being the most known, common, and analogically predicated.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that absolute existence is a concrete universal that exists externally as a single entity shared by all things.
Correction: The passage clarifies that absolute existence is a mental concept (mental predicate and secondary intelligible), not a self-subsistent external reality. It cannot be the Necessary Being because it lacks independent existence and is divisible, multiple, and analogical.

Key Takeaway
Absolute existence is a mental abstraction with divisible, multiple, and analogical properties, making it impossible for it to be the unique, necessary, and indivisible Necessary Being.

Why the Necessary Being is Not Absolute Existence
Refutation of identifying the Necessary Being with absolute existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why identifying the Necessary Being (al-wajib) with absolute existence (al-wujud al-mutlaq) is philosophically and theologically untenable, and how the author refutes it by showing that such a view leads to contradictions with established rational and revealed principles.

Core Idea
Absolute existence is a mental concept; God is real, not a mental abstraction.

This lesson examines a key refutation in Islamic theology: the claim that God is simply 'absolute existence.' The author argues that this view rests on misunderstanding the nature of existence as a mental predicate and leads to absurd conclusions. By the end, you'll see why the Necessary Being must be understood as a concrete, unique reality with attributes, not a generic concept.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the logical flow: it first discusses mental predicates, then divisions of existence, then an objection and reply, then the conclusion.
The passage is dense; don't worry about every detail at first.
2
Identify the core claim being refuted
The passage targets the idea that the Necessary Being is identical to absolute existence. Underline the phrase 'الوجود المطلق' and note the author's main counter-arguments.
Look for what the author calls 'corrupt principles' (أصول فاسدة).
3
Examine the objection and the author's response
The objection claims the subject is independent of existence. The author replies that the relation is mental. Reflect on how this supports the refutation.
This shows that absolute existence does not inhere in external reality.
4
Understand the conclusion
The author summarizes that the claim rests on false principles and contradicts agreed-upon truths, like God being the source of existence and having attributes. Write down three consequences he lists.
This ties to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في الخارج، كالكلية والجزئية والذاتية والعرضية، لأنها أمور تلحق حقائق الأشياء عند حصولها في العقل وليس في الأعيان شيء هو الوجود أو الذاتية أو العرضية مثلاً. وإنما في الأعيان الإنسان والسواد مثلاً وههنا نظر من جهة أن ما انساق إليه البيان هو أن وجودات الأشياء من المحمولات العقلية والمعقولات الثانية وكان الكلام في الوجود المطلق، ومنها أنه ينقسم إلى الواجب والممكن، لأنه إن كان مفتقراً إلى سبب فممكن وإلا فواجب وإلى القديم والحادث، لأنه إن كان مسبوقاً بالغير أو بالعدم فحادث وإلا فقـديم، ومنها أنه يتكثر بتكثر الموضوعات الشخصية كوجود زيد وعمرو والنوعية كوجود الإنسان والفرس، والجنسية كوجود الحيوان والنبات . فإن قيل : الموضوع هو المحل المستغني في قوامه عن ذلك للوجود . الحال ولا يتصور قلنا : المراد ههنا ما يقابل المحمول وهو الذي يحمل عليه الوجود بالاشتقاق، ولو سلم فالقيام ههنا عقلي، والماهية تلاحظ دون الوجود، وهذا معنى استغنائه عن العارض، وإن كان لا ينفك عن وجود عقلي، وظاهر هذا الكلام أن وجودات الممكنات إنما هي نفس الوجود المطلق، تكثرت بالإضافة إلى المحل، وليست أموراً متكثرة متخصصة بأنفسها معروضة له، وكان المراد أن الوجود المطلق يتكثر ما صدق هو عليه من الوجودات الخاصة بتكثر الموضوعات ومنها أنه مقول على الوجودات بالتشكيك، كما سبق. وجميع ذلك مما يستحيل في حق الواجب تعالى وتقدس. وبالجملة فالقول بكون الواجب هو الوجود المطلق مبني على أصول فاسدة، مثل كونه واحداً بالشخصي موجوداً في الخارج ممتنع العدم لذاته ومستلزم لبطلان أمور اتفق العقلاء عليها، مثل كونه أعرف الأشياء مشتركاً بين الوجودات مقولاً عليها بالتشكيك معدوداً في ثواني المعقولات، وكون الواجب مبدأ لوجود الممكنات متصفاً بالعلم والقدرة والإرادة والحياة وإرسال الرسل، وإنزال الكتب، وغير ذلك بما وردت به الشريعة.
In the external world, like universality and particularity and essentiality and accidentally, because they are matters that attach to the realities of things when they occur in the mind, and there is nothing in external entities that is existence or essentiality or accidentally, for example. Rather, in external entities there is man and blackness, for example. And here there is consideration from the aspect that what the exposition leads to is that the existences of things are among the mental predicates and secondary intelligibles, and the discussion was about absolute existence. And among them (the points) is that it divides into the necessary and the possible, because if it is in need of a cause then it is possible, otherwise it is necessary; and into the eternal and the originated, because if it is preceded by another or by non-existence then it is originated, otherwise it is eternal. And among them is that it multiplies by the multiplicity of individual subjects like the existence of Zayd and Amr, and specific like the existence of man and horse, and generic like the existence of animal and plant. For if it is said: The subject is the locus that is independent in its constitution from that existence; the state is not conceivable. We say: What is meant here is what is opposed to the predicate, and it is that upon which existence is predicated derivationally. And even if it is granted, then the inherence here is mental, and the quiddity is observed without existence, and this is the meaning of its independence from the accident, even if it is not free from mental existence. And the apparent meaning of this speech is that the existences of possibles are themselves absolute existence, multiplied by relation to the locus, and they are not multiple things specialized in themselves serving as subjects for it. And what was meant is that absolute existence multiplies according to the particular existences that it applies to by the multiplicity of subjects. And among them is that it is predicated of existences by analogy (tashkik), as previously. And all of that is impossible with respect to the Necessary Being, exalted and sanctified. And in summary, the statement that the Necessary Being is absolute existence is based on corrupt principles, such as it being individually one, existing in the external, impossible of non-existence by itself, and it entails the invalidation of matters upon which the rational ones agree, such as it being the most known of things, common among existences, predicated of them by analogy, counted among the secondary intelligibles, and that the Necessary Being is the source of the existence of possibles, qualified by knowledge, power, will, life, sending messengers, revealing books, and other things that have come in the Sharia.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage refutes the view that the Necessary Being (al-wajib) is identical to absolute existence (al-wujud al-mutlaq). It begins by explaining that attributes like universality, particularity, essentiality, and accidentally are mental considerations, not external realities. The author then notes that the preceding discussion treats existences as mental predicates and secondary intelligibles, and that absolute existence is divided into necessary and contingent, eternal and originated, and multiplies by subjects. An objection is raised: the subject (mahall) is independent in its constitution from existence, so how can existence inhere? The answer distinguishes between the subject as a locus and the logical subject of predication; the inherence is mental, and quiddity is considered without existence. This implies that contingent existences are nothing but absolute existence multiplied by relation to loci. The author rejects this, stating that all such properties are impossible for the Necessary Being. The conclusion is that identifying the Wajib with absolute existence rests on false principles, such as being individually one and existing externally, and leads to the denial of agreed-upon truths—that the Wajib is most known, common to existences, predicated analogically, a secondary intelligible, and the source of contingent existences with attributes like knowledge, power, will, life, etc. This argument shows the error of a prevalent philosophical view.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Necessary Being is a simple, absolute existence without attributes, identical to the concept of existence itself.
Correction: The passage shows that absolute existence is a mental concept that divides, multiplies, and is predicated by analogy, all impossible for God. Moreover, it would negate the attributes of God as Creator, Knower, etc.

Key Takeaway

The Initial Positions on the Existence of Existence
Two positions on existence and the regress argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two initial positions on whether existence itself exists and the infinite regress argument against real existence.

Core Idea
Existence cannot exist without leading to infinite regress or equivocity.

This passage opens a deep debate: does the concept of existence itself have a real existence? Two opposing views are immediately set forth. The first says existence exists by its own nature; the second argues it is a mere mental consideration, because positing real existence leads to an infinite regress. Let us follow the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the two positions: 'قيل: موجود بوجود هو نفسه' and 'قيل: بل اعتباري محض'.
The first position claims existence exists without additional existence.
2
Identify the infinite regress argument
The second position argues: if existence existed, it would require either an additional existence (regress) or be identical to its own existence (equivocal predication).
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: why is this argument important for theology? It challenges whether existence is a real attribute or a mental concept.
This sets the stage for later discussions about God's essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في تقدمه وتحققه عن الوجود، ومنها اختلافهم في أنه موجود أو لا فقيل : موجود بوجود هو نفسه فلا يتسلسل . وقيل : بل اعتباري محض لا تحقق له في الأعيان إذ لو وجد فإما أن يوجد بوجود زائد فيتسلسل أو بوجود هو نفسه فلا يكون إطلاق الموجود على الوجود وعلى سائر الأشياء بمعنى واحد، لأن معناه في الوجود أنه الوجود، وفي غيره أنه ذو الوجود، ولأنه إما أن يكون جوهراً فلا يقع صفة للأشياء، أو عرضاً فيتقوم المحل دونه والتقوم بدون الوجود محال، ولأن ما ذكر في زيادة الوجود على الماهية من أنا نعقل الماهية ونشك في وجودها جار بعينه في وجود الوجود فإنا نعقل الوجود ونشك في وجوده فلو وجد لكان وجوده زائداً وتسلسل . وبهذا يتبين بطلان ما ذهب إليه الفلاسفة من أن ماهية الواجب نفس الوجود المجرد . وذلك لأنا بعد ما نتصور الوجود المجرد نطلب بالبرهان وجوده في الأعيان، فيكون وجوده زائداً ويتسلسل ولا محيص إلا بأن الوجود المقول على الوجودات اعتبار عقلي كما سبق . وقيل : الوجود ليس بموجود ولا معدوم، بل واسطة على ما سيأتي .
In its precedence and realization over existence, and among them is their disagreement over whether it exists or not. It was said: it exists by an existence that is itself, so there is no infinite regress. And it was said: rather it is a pure mental consideration with no realization in external entities, because if it existed, then either it would exist by an additional existence leading to infinite regress, or by an existence that is itself, in which case the application of 'existent' to existence and to other things would not be in one sense, because its meaning in existence is that it is existence, and in other things that it possesses existence, and because it would either be a substance and then not occur as an attribute of things, or an accident and then the substrate would be constituted without it, and constitution without existence is impossible, and because what was mentioned regarding the addition of existence to essence — that we conceive the essence and doubt its existence — applies exactly to the existence of existence, for we conceive existence and doubt its existence, so if it existed, its existence would be additional and lead to infinite regress. And by this the falsity of what the philosophers held — that the essence of the Necessary Being is pure existence — becomes clear. That is because after we conceive pure existence, we seek by proof its existence in external entities, so its existence would be additional and lead to infinite regress, and there is no escape except that existence predicated of existences is a mental consideration, as earlier. And it was said: existence is neither existent nor non-existent, rather an intermediary, as will come.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a dense kalam argument about whether existence itself exists. The author begins by noting that among the disagreements about existence is whether it exists or not. Two positions are given: (1) it exists by an existence that is itself, thus no regress; (2) it is a pure mental consideration with no external reality. The second position is argued: if existence existed, it would either need an additional existence (leading to regress) or be its own existence (making the term 'existent' equivocal). Further objections are raised: if existence is a substance, it cannot be a predicate; if an accident, it would require a substrate that exists without it, which is impossible. The author then strengthens the argument by analogy: just as we conceive an essence and doubt its existence, so we conceive existence and doubt its existence, implying that existence must have an additional existence, leading to regress. This refutes the philosophers' claim that the Necessary Being's essence is pure existence, because after conceiving pure existence, we still need to prove its external existence, which would be additional and cause regress. The only way out is to consider existence predicated of existences as a mental consideration. Finally, a third view is mentioned: existence is neither existent nor non-existent but an intermediary.

The dilemma that existence cannot be real without leading to regress or equivocity forces a mental-consideration view.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson argues that the term 'existent' cannot apply in the same way to existence itself as it does to created things. Does this challenge the way you think about Allah's existence as 'existent'? Are you comfortable with the idea that human logic reaches its limit here, or do you feel a need to reconcile this with your faith? Commit to reading the Quranic verses about Allah's existence with this tension in mind.
?
The second position concludes that existence is merely a mental consideration. If that is true, what does that say about the reality of the world around you? Is everything, in a sense, a concept? How does this affect your confidence in the physical evidence for God? Take a moment to ponder where you place your ultimate certainty—in reasoned proofs or in the direct experience of faith?
?
The dilemma shows that either infinite regress or equivocity follows if existence is real. Both are unacceptable in kalam. When you face a logical puzzle in your faith that seems to have no clean answer, do you submit to revelation or try to force a human solution? This week, when you struggle with a theological difficulty, resolve to pause and say, 'I hold to what the Quran and Sunnah say,' even if my mind cannot fully grasp it.

Arguments Against Existence as Real: Substance, Accident, and Analogy
Substance/accident argument and regress from the essence-existence distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the additional arguments that existence cannot be a real attribute: it cannot be a substance or an accident, and the analogy with essence leads to regress.

Core Idea
Existence, if real, would be neither substance nor accident, and an infinite regress follows.

The previous lesson presented the dilemma of regress or equivocity. Now the author deepens the critique: if existence were real, what ontological category could it belong to? Neither substance nor accident fits. Moreover, the famous argument that existence is additional to essence is applied to existence itself, generating a vicious regress. Let us follow these arguments step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage which continues the second position's arguments. Focus on the three reasons: meaning, substance/accident, and the analogy with essence.
The passage begins with 'لأن معناه في الوجود أنه الوجود'.
2
Analyze the substance/accident argument
If existence is a substance, it cannot be a predicate (attribute) of things. If it is an accident, it needs a substrate that exists without it, which is impossible.
3
Understand the analogy argument
Just as we conceive an essence and doubt its existence, we conceive existence and doubt its existence. If existence is real, its existence would be additional, leading to regress.
This is a powerful argument that will be used against the philosophers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في تقدمه وتحققه عن الوجود، ومنها اختلافهم في أنه موجود أو لا فقيل : موجود بوجود هو نفسه فلا يتسلسل . وقيل : بل اعتباري محض لا تحقق له في الأعيان إذ لو وجد فإما أن يوجد بوجود زائد فيتسلسل أو بوجود هو نفسه فلا يكون إطلاق الموجود على الوجود وعلى سائر الأشياء بمعنى واحد، لأن معناه في الوجود أنه الوجود، وفي غيره أنه ذو الوجود، ولأنه إما أن يكون جوهراً فلا يقع صفة للأشياء، أو عرضاً فيتقوم المحل دونه والتقوم بدون الوجود محال، ولأن ما ذكر في زيادة الوجود على الماهية من أنا نعقل الماهية ونشك في وجودها جار بعينه في وجود الوجود فإنا نعقل الوجود ونشك في وجوده فلو وجد لكان وجوده زائداً وتسلسل . وبهذا يتبين بطلان ما ذهب إليه الفلاسفة من أن ماهية الواجب نفس الوجود المجرد . وذلك لأنا بعد ما نتصور الوجود المجرد نطلب بالبرهان وجوده في الأعيان، فيكون وجوده زائداً ويتسلسل ولا محيص إلا بأن الوجود المقول على الوجودات اعتبار عقلي كما سبق . وقيل : الوجود ليس بموجود ولا معدوم، بل واسطة على ما سيأتي .
In its precedence and realization over existence, and among them is their disagreement over whether it exists or not. It was said: it exists by an existence that is itself, so there is no infinite regress. And it was said: rather it is a pure mental consideration with no realization in external entities, because if it existed, then either it would exist by an additional existence leading to infinite regress, or by an existence that is itself, in which case the application of 'existent' to existence and to other things would not be in one sense, because its meaning in existence is that it is existence, and in other things that it possesses existence, and because it would either be a substance and then not occur as an attribute of things, or an accident and then the substrate would be constituted without it, and constitution without existence is impossible, and because what was mentioned regarding the addition of existence to essence — that we conceive the essence and doubt its existence — applies exactly to the existence of existence, for we conceive existence and doubt its existence, so if it existed, its existence would be additional and lead to infinite regress. And by this the falsity of what the philosophers held — that the essence of the Necessary Being is pure existence — becomes clear. That is because after we conceive pure existence, we seek by proof its existence in external entities, so its existence would be additional and lead to infinite regress, and there is no escape except that existence predicated of existences is a mental consideration, as earlier. And it was said: existence is neither existent nor non-existent, rather an intermediary, as will come.

Commentary
This passage is a dense kalam argument about whether existence itself exists. The author begins by noting that among the disagreements about existence is whether it exists or not. Two positions are given: (1) it exists by an existence that is itself, thus no regress; (2) it is a pure mental consideration with no external reality. The only way out is to consider existence predicated of existences as a mental consideration. Finally, a third view is mentioned: existence is neither existent nor non-existent but an intermediary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The argument forces a strict dichotomy: existence must be either substance or accident. If it were an accident, it would require a pre-existing substrate, but nothing can exist without existence. Have you ever caught yourself thinking that you 'have' existence as if it were a property you own? How does this passage challenge that assumption?
?
An infinite regress would follow if existence were real. In your life, do you ever try to ground your own worth or identity in things that are themselves contingent? What would it mean for you to stop that regress and rest solely in the Necessary Being?

Refuting the Philosophers and the Third View
Refutation of philosophers' view and introduction of the intermediary view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the previous arguments refute the philosophers' claim that God's essence is pure existence, and the alternative view that existence is an intermediary.

Core Idea
The philosophers' view of God as pure existence is refuted by the regress argument.

Having established that existence cannot be real, the author now applies this to a major theological claim: the philosophers (Falasifa) argue that the Necessary Being's essence is pure existence. Using the same reasoning, the author shows this leads to an infinite regress. The only way out, he says, is to consider existence a mental consideration. Finally, a third view is mentioned: existence is neither existent nor non-existent but an intermediate state. Let us see how the argument concludes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage that begins with 'وبهذا يتبين بطلان ما ذهب إليه الفلاسفة'. Follow the reasoning from conceiving pure existence to seeking proof of its external existence.
2
Understand the refutation
The author argues that after conceiving pure existence, we still need a proof that it exists externally. That proof would require an additional existence, leading to regress.
This directly challenges the philosophers' identification of God's essence with existence.
3
Consider the third view
The final sentence mentions a third position: existence is an intermediary (neither existent nor non-existent). This will be explained later.
This shows the debate was not settled, but the author likely favors the mental consideration view.

The Power Argument Against Thubut al-Ma'dum
Al-Taftazani presents and refutes the power-based argument against thubut al-ma'dum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that thubut al-ma'dum would negate divine power and the initial refutation that power acts on the qualification of essence with existence.

Core Idea
Divine power does not require denying thubut al-ma'dum.

Al-Taftazani presents a key argument from his opponents: if non-existents are fixed, then God's power cannot affect them. This lesson unpacks that argument and shows how the response opens a different perspective—power applies to the relationship between essence and existence, not to the essence itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponent's claim
Read the passage carefully and identify the claim that thubut al-ma'dum would make divine power impossible over possibles.
The argument is presented as a proof from existence.
2
Analyze the argument structure
Notice the dichotomy: the effect of power must be either on the essence (eternal, thus not subject to power) or on existence (a state, not subject to power).
The argument assumes states are not subject to power.
3
Understand the response
The response denies the exclusivity of the dichotomy, asserting that power acts on the qualification of the essence with existence.
This qualification is not a state in the problematic sense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منا من جعل نفي ثبوت المعدوم غير ضروري فاستدل عليه بوجوده. الأول: لو كان المعدوم ثابتاً لامتنع تأثير القدرة في شيء من الممكنات واللازم باطل ضرورة واتفاقاً. وجه اللزوم أن التأثير إما في نفس الذات وهي أزلية والأزلية تنافي المقدورية. وإما في الوجود وهو حال إما على المثبتين فإلزاماً، وإما على النافين فإثباتاً بالحجة على ما سيأتي . والأحوال ليست بمقدورة باتفاق القائلين بها ولأن عدم توقف لونية السواد وعالمية من فام به العلم على تأثير القدرة ضروري، وأما التمسك بأنه لو كان مثل عالمية العالم، ومتحركية المتحرك بالفاعل، لكن (١) بدون العلم والحركة ويؤدي إلى إبطال القول بالأعراض، فلا يخفى ضعفه، ثم نفي المقدورية لا يستلزم ثبوت الأزلية، ليلزم أزليه الوجود، بل أزلية اتصاف الذات بالوجود بناء على كونه نسبة بينهما، لا يتوقف على غيرهما لأنهم يجوزون الثبوت بلا علة أو بعلة غير قادرة . وأجيب بمنع الحصر لجواز أن يكون تأثير القدرة في اتصاف الذات بالوجود، لا يقال الاتصاف منتف . أما أولاً : فلأنه لو ثبت لكان له اتصاف بثبوت وتسلسل . بحسب وأما ثانياً : فلما سبق من أنه ليس بين الماهية والوجود اتصاف الخارج، كما بين البياض والجسم وإنما ذلك بحسب الذهن فقط، وإلا لزم اتصاف المعدوم بالوجود، لأن الماهية بدون الوجود لا تكون بحسب الخارج إلا معدومة، إذ الماهية من حيث هي هي إنما هي (٢) في التصور فقط لأنا نجيب عن الأول : بأنه لو سلم زيادة اتصاف الاتصاف بالثبوت على نفس الاتصاف، فلا نسلم (٣) نفي (٤) استحالة التسلسل في الثابتات وإنما قام الدليل عليه في الموجودات . وعن الثاني : بأنا لا نسلم (٥) استحالة اتصاف المعدوم الثابت بالوجود، وصيرورته عند الاتصاف موجوداً بذلك الوجود، كالجسم الغير الأسود يتصف بالسواد، ويصير أسود بذلك السواد، وإنما يستحيل ذلك فيما ليس بثابت في الخارج، وهذا ما ذكره الإمام من أن القول بثبوت المعدوم متفرع على :
Among us is one who made the negation of the fixedness of the non-existent not self-evident, so he adduced evidence for it by way of [the argument of] existence. The first: if the non-existent were fixed, then the effect of power would be impossible in any of the possibles—and the consequent is false necessarily and by agreement. The manner of the entailment is that the effect is either in the very essence, which is eternal, and eternality contradicts being subject to power; or in existence, which is a state (ḥāl). For the affirmers [of states] it is by way of entailment, and for the deniers it is by way of proof according to what will come. And states (aḥwāl) are not subject to power by agreement of those who affirm them, and because the non-dependence of the blackness-attribute of black and the knowledge-attribute of the one who knows on the effect of power is self-evident. As for the clinging to the [claim] that if it were like the knowledge-attribute of the knower and the motion-attribute of the mover by the agent, but without knowledge and motion, and it leads to the invalidation of the doctrine of accidents, its weakness is not hidden. Then, the negation of being subject to power does not necessitate the affirmation of eternality, so that the eternality of existence would be necessitated; rather, the eternality of the qualification of the essence with existence, based on its being a relation between them, does not depend on anything else, because they allow fixedness without a cause or with a non-powerful cause. And it was answered: by denying the exclusivity, for it is permissible that the effect of power is in the qualification of the essence with existence. It should not be said that the qualification is negated. As for the first [objection against this]: because if it were fixed, it would have a qualification with fixedness and infinite regress, accordingly. As for the second: because of what preceded, that there is no external qualification between the quiddity (māhiyya) and existence, as between whiteness and body; rather, that is only in the mind. Otherwise, the qualification of the non-existent with existence would be necessitated, because the quiddity without existence is not, in the external, except non-existent, since the quiddity in itself is only in conception. For we answer the first [objection]: by [saying] that even if we grant an additional qualification of the qualification with fixedness beyond the qualification itself, we do not concede the denial of the impossibility of infinite regress in fixed things; rather, the proof for that [impossibility] is only established for existents. And as for the second: by [saying] that we do not concede the impossibility of the qualification of the fixed non-existent with existence, and its becoming, upon qualification, existent by that existence, like the non-black body that is qualified with blackness and becomes black by that blackness. That is only impossible for what is not fixed in the external. And this is what the Imām mentioned, that the doctrine of the fixedness of the non-existent is based on:
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes an argument against thubut al-ma'dum based on divine power. The argument goes: if non-existents are fixed, then God's power cannot affect them, because power either acts on the essence (which is eternal, contradicting contingency) or on its existence (which is a state, and states are not subject to power). The consequent is false, so thubut is false. The response denies the exclusive dichotomy: power can affect the qualification of the essence with existence, which is not a state in the problematic sense. The objections to this response are answered: infinite regress in fixed things is not impossible, and the qualification of a fixed non-existent with existence is analogous to a body acquiring blackness—possible for what is fixed externally. The passage concludes by noting that the doctrine of thubut al-ma'dum is based on a certain foundation (which is cut off at the page break). The overall purpose is to show that divine power is not negated by thubut al-ma'dum.

Key Terms
ثبوت المعدوم (thubut al-ma'dum)
القدرة (al-qudra)
الحال (al-ḥāl)
الاتصاف (al-ittiṣāf)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think thubut al-ma'dum implies God cannot create because the non-existent already has a fixed reality.
Correction: The refutation shows that power acts on the relationship between essence and existence, so creating is bringing about that relationship, not altering a fixed entity.

Checkpoint
According to the response, what is the proper locus of divine power?
A) The essence of the possible itself.
B) The existence of the possible as a state.
C) The qualification of the essence with existence.
D) The non-existent as such.

Key Takeaway
The power of the Creator is not impeded by the fixedness of non-existents, because power works on the qualification of essence with existence, not on the essence itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever feel that your bad habits are an unchangeable part of your essence? How does the truth that God's power works on qualification, not essence, challenge that feeling and invite you to seek real change?
?
When you think about your future, do you secretly doubt that God can change the course of your life because you feel 'fixed'? How does the refutation of the power argument give you hope that your state can be transformed?
?
Are there areas in your life where you have resigned yourself to thinking 'this is just how I am'? How does the concept of ittiṣāf call you to ask God to change not who you are, but how you are?

Objections to the Refutation and Their Answers
Al-Taftazani addresses objections to the refutation of the power argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main objections raised against the refutation and how al-Taftazani answers them.

Core Idea
Facing objections strengthens the doctrine of thubut al-ma'dum.

The response to the power argument—that power acts on qualification—faces two immediate objections: it would entail an infinite regress of qualifications, and it would require an external relation between quiddity and existence. Al-Taftazani addresses both, showing that infinite regress in fixed things is not impossible and that qualification can occur for fixed non-existents analogously to a body acquiring blackness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two objections
Read the passage starting from 'لا يقال الاتصاف منتف' and note the two objections: infinite regress and lack of external relation.
The objections are introduced with 'أما أولاً' and 'أما ثانياً'.
2
Examine the first answer
See how al-Taftazani responds to the infinite regress objection by denying its impossibility in fixed things.
The proof against infinite regress applies only to existents.
3
Examine the second answer
Understand the analogy of a body acquiring blackness to show that a fixed non-existent can be qualified with existence.
This is possible because the non-existent is fixed externally.
4
Reflect on the broader implication
Consider how these answers reinforce the doctrine of thubut al-ma'dum and its foundation.
The passage ends with a reference to the Imam's foundation, though cut off.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منا من جعل نفي ثبوت المعدوم غير ضروري فاستدل عليه بوجوده. الأول: لو كان المعدوم ثابتاً لامتنع تأثير القدرة في شيء من الممكنات واللازم باطل ضرورة واتفاقاً. وجه اللزوم أن التأثير إما في نفس الذات وهي أزلية والأزلية تنافي المقدورية. وإما في الوجود وهو حال إما على المثبتين فإلزاماً، وإما على النافين فإثباتاً بالحجة على ما سيأتي . والأحوال ليست بمقدورة باتفاق القائلين بها ولأن عدم توقف لونية السواد وعالمية من فام به العلم على تأثير القدرة ضروري، وأما التمسك بأنه لو كان مثل عالمية العالم، ومتحركية المتحرك بالفاعل، لكن (١) بدون العلم والحركة ويؤدي إلى إبطال القول بالأعراض، فلا يخفى ضعفه، ثم نفي المقدورية لا يستلزم ثبوت الأزلية، ليلزم أزليه الوجود، بل أزلية اتصاف الذات بالوجود بناء على كونه نسبة بينهما، لا يتوقف على غيرهما لأنهم يجوزون الثبوت بلا علة أو بعلة غير قادرة . وأجيب بمنع الحصر لجواز أن يكون تأثير القدرة في اتصاف الذات بالوجود، لا يقال الاتصاف منتف . أما أولاً : فلأنه لو ثبت لكان له اتصاف بثبوت وتسلسل . بحسب وأما ثانياً : فلما سبق من أنه ليس بين الماهية والوجود اتصاف الخارج، كما بين البياض والجسم وإنما ذلك بحسب الذهن فقط، وإلا لزم اتصاف المعدوم بالوجود، لأن الماهية بدون الوجود لا تكون بحسب الخارج إلا معدومة، إذ الماهية من حيث هي هي إنما هي (٢) في التصور فقط لأنا نجيب عن الأول : بأنه لو سلم زيادة اتصاف الاتصاف بالثبوت على نفس الاتصاف، فلا نسلم (٣) نفي (٤) استحالة التسلسل في الثابتات وإنما قام الدليل عليه في الموجودات . وعن الثاني : بأنا لا نسلم (٥) استحالة اتصاف المعدوم الثابت بالوجود، وصيرورته عند الاتصاف موجوداً بذلك الوجود، كالجسم الغير الأسود يتصف بالسواد، ويصير أسود بذلك السواد، وإنما يستحيل ذلك فيما ليس بثابت في الخارج، وهذا ما ذكره الإمام من أن القول بثبوت المعدوم متفرع على :
Among us is one who made the negation of the fixedness of the non-existent not self-evident, so he adduced evidence for it by way of [the argument of] existence. The first: if the non-existent were fixed, then the effect of power would be impossible in any of the possibles—and the consequent is false necessarily and by agreement. The manner of the entailment is that the effect is either in the very essence, which is eternal, and eternality contradicts being subject to power; or in existence, which is a state (ḥāl). For the affirmers [of states] it is by way of entailment, and for the deniers it is by way of proof according to what will come. And states (aḥwāl) are not subject to power by agreement of those who affirm them, and because the non-dependence of the blackness-attribute of black and the knowledge-attribute of the one who knows on the effect of power is self-evident. As for the clinging to the [claim] that if it were like the knowledge-attribute of the knower and the motion-attribute of the mover by the agent, but without knowledge and motion, and it leads to the invalidation of the doctrine of accidents, its weakness is not hidden. Then, the negation of being subject to power does not necessitate the affirmation of eternality, so that the eternality of existence would be necessitated; rather, the eternality of the qualification of the essence with existence, based on its being a relation between them, does not depend on anything else, because they allow fixedness without a cause or with a non-powerful cause. And it was answered: by denying the exclusivity, for it is permissible that the effect of power is in the qualification of the essence with existence. It should not be said that the qualification is negated. As for the first [objection against this]: because if it were fixed, it would have a qualification with fixedness and infinite regress, accordingly. As for the second: because of what preceded, that there is no external qualification between the quiddity (māhiyya) and existence, as between whiteness and body; rather, that is only in the mind. Otherwise, the qualification of the non-existent with existence would be necessitated, because the quiddity without existence is not, in the external, except non-existent, since the quiddity in itself is only in conception. For we answer the first [objection]: by [saying] that even if we grant an additional qualification of the qualification with fixedness beyond the qualification itself, we do not concede the denial of the impossibility of infinite regress in fixed things; rather, the proof for that [impossibility] is only established for existents. And as for the second: by [saying] that we do not concede the impossibility of the qualification of the fixed non-existent with existence, and its becoming, upon qualification, existent by that existence, like the non-black body that is qualified with blackness and becomes black by that blackness. That is only impossible for what is not fixed in the external. And this is what the Imām mentioned, that the doctrine of the fixedness of the non-existent is based on:
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes an argument against thubut al-ma'dum based on divine power. The argument goes: if non-existents are fixed, then God's power cannot affect them, because power either acts on the essence (which is eternal, contradicting contingency) or on its existence (which is a state, and states are not subject to power). The consequent is false, so thubut is false. The response denies the exclusive dichotomy: power can affect the qualification of the essence with existence, which is not a state in the problematic sense. The objections to this response are answered: infinite regress in fixed things is not impossible, and the qualification of a fixed non-existent with existence is analogous to a body acquiring blackness—possible for what is fixed externally. The passage concludes by noting that the doctrine of thubut al-ma'dum is based on a certain foundation (which is cut off at the page break). The overall purpose is to show that divine power is not negated by thubut al-ma'dum.

Key Terms
الاتصاف (al-ittiṣāf)
التسلسل (al-tasalsul)
الماهية (al-māhiyya)
الوجود (al-wujūd)
الخارج (al-khārij)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if the qualification is a relation, then it would require an infinite chain of relations.
Correction: The response clarifies that infinite regress is not problematic for fixed (non-existent) things, only for existents.

Checkpoint
How does al-Taftazani answer the objection that a fixed non-existent cannot be qualified with existence?
A) He denies that the non-existent is fixed.
B) He uses the analogy of a body acquiring blackness.
C) He says such qualification is only mental.
D) He argues that power is not involved.

Key Takeaway
Al-Taftazani defends thubut al-ma'dum by showing that objections based on infinite regress and the nature of relations do not hold, as the rules for fixed non-existents differ from those for existents.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter intellectual objections to your beliefs, do you dismiss them quickly or engage deeply as al-Taftazani did? How can you cultivate a patient, analytical approach to defending your faith?
?
The concept of 'fixed non-existents' reminds us that God knows all things before they exist. Does this truth change how you entrust your future to Allah, or do you still worry about unknowns?
?
This lesson shows that not all infinite regresses are equal—some are impossible, others are not. Where in your own thinking might you be applying a rule too broadly, missing the nuance of a situation? How can you seek deeper understanding?

Objection and Answer: Essences Would Be Necessary if Established in Non-Existence
Objection and answer about essences becoming necessary if established in non-existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third objection against thubut al-ma'dum and why it fails, clarifying that essences can be established in non-existence without being necessary.

Core Idea
Establishment in non-existence does not make essences necessary; it only means they are preceded by negation.

This lesson tackles a sophisticated objection: if essences (dhawāt) are established in non-existence without deriving their establishment from another, they would be necessary (wājib), leading to multiple necessary beings. The author then answers by showing that the objection only proves they are preceded by negation, not that their thubut in non-existence is impossible. Follow the reasoning step by step to see how kalam defends its position.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation, focusing on the conditional statement: 'if essences were established in non-existence... they would be necessary.' Notice the logic and the conclusion of multiplicity.
The objection equates establishment from other than itself with necessity.
2
Examine the two-part exposition
The objector explains that if essences are established, their establishment is either necessary (leading to multiple necessary beings) or possible (making them originated and preceded by negation). Understand both branches.
The second branch leads to the claim that essences as such are preceded by negation.
3
Understand the author's answer
The author responds that even if we accept that every possible of establishment is originated, that only shows that essences are preceded by negation. It does not negate that they are established without existence.
The key distinction: 'preceded by negation' is not the same as 'non-existent'.
4
Reflect on the logical move
Notice that the author does not reject the premise that every possible is originated; rather, he denies that this entails the impossibility of thubut in non-existence. The objection confuses 'preceded by negation' with 'not established'.
This shows the subtlety of kalam reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث : لو كانت الذوات ثابتة في العدم وعندكم أن ثبوتها ليس من غيرها كانت واجبة، إذ لا معنى للواجب سوى هذا ، فيلزم وجوب الممكنات، وتعدد الواجب. وتقريرهم أنها لو كانت ثابتة فثبوتها إما واجب فيتعدد الواجب، أو ممكن فيكون محدثاً مسبوقاً بالنفي، فتكون الذوات من حيث هي مسبوقة بالنفي، وهو مع ابتنائه على كون كل ممكن الثبوت محدثاً، بمعنى المسبوق بالنفي لا ينفي كون الذوات ثابتة بدون الوجود، بل غايته أن ثبوتها في العدم مسبوق بنفيها .
The third: if the essences (dhawāt) were established in non-existence, and according to you their establishment is not from other than them, they would be necessary, for there is no meaning of 'necessary' other than this. Then the necessity of possibles and the multiplicity of the Necessary would follow. And their exposition: if they were established, their establishment is either necessary, then the Necessary would be multiple, or possible, then it would be originated (muḥdath) preceded by negation. Therefore the essences as such are preceded by negation. And this, along with its being based on the fact that every possible of establishment is originated, meaning preceded by negation, does not negate that the essences are established without existence; rather, its utmost is that their establishment in non-existence is preceded by their negation.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage presents the third objection and its answer. The objector argues that if essences (dhawāt) are established in non-existence, and their establishment does not come from another, then they would be necessary (wājiba), leading to the necessity of all possible things and the multiplicity of the Necessary Being. The explanation is that if they are established, their establishment is either necessary (leading to multiple necessary beings) or possible, in which case they would be originated (muḥdath) and preceded by negation (i.e., they did not exist before). Thus the essences as such are preceded by negation. The author responds that even if we accept this reasoning, it does not negate that the essences are established without existence. The utmost it shows is that their thubut in non-existence is preceded by their non-existence, not that they cannot be established in non-existence.

Key Terms
الذوات
ثبوت
العدم
الواجب
الممكن
المحدث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That thubut al-ma'dum inevitably leads to multiple necessary beings, proving the doctrine false.
Correction: The author shows that the objection only demonstrates that essences in non-existence are preceded by negation, not that they are necessary or that multiple necessary beings exist. The doctrine remains intact.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if essences are established in non-existence and their establishment is not from another?
A) They become impossible.
B) They become necessary.
C) They become contingent.
D) They become eternal.

Key Takeaway
The objection that essences would be necessary if established in non-existence fails because it only shows they are preceded by negation, not that they cannot be established without existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

How does realizing that everything about you is preceded by absolute non-existence (you were nothing) change the way you see yourself before Allah?
?
The objector feared that multiple things could become necessary; the author showed they are still possible and preceded by negation. When you feel pride in your good deeds or your faith, do you remember that even those are possible, not necessary, and that you are utterly dependent on Allah for their existence?
?
If you truly internalized that your very existence is established only by Allah's will and not from yourself, what specific habit or attitude in your daily life would you change today? Commit to one concrete action that reflects this dependence.

The Objection of Necessary Essences and the Response Defining Necessity
Presents the objection and response regarding fixed essences and necessity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that fixed non-existent essences would be necessary and the key distinction between necessity in existence and necessity in fixation.

Core Idea
Necessity belongs to existence, not to mere fixity.

The third objection attempts to prove that if essences are fixed in non-existence without external cause, they would be necessary, leading to absurdities. The response hinges on a precise definition of necessary being. Let's examine the argument and its resolution.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully once, then read the English translation. Notice the flow: objection, elaboration, answer.
The passage is compact; pay attention to each conditional statement.
2
Identify the three parts
The passage has three sections: the objection (if essences are fixed...), the elaboration (either necessary or possible), and the answer (the necessary is independent in existence, not fixity).
The elaboration includes a discussion of 'preceded by negation'.
3
Understand the resolution
The answer refines the definition of 'necessary'. Ask yourself: why does this distinction between existence and fixity defeat the objection?
Fixity (thubut) is a broader concept than existence; it includes both necessary and possible things.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث : لو كانت الذوات ثابتة في العدم وعندكم أن ثبوتها ليس من غيرها كانت واجبة، إذ لا معنى للواجب سوى هذا ، فيلزم وجوب الممكنات، وتعدد الواجب. وتقريرهم أنها لو كانت ثابتة فثبوتها إما واجب فيتعدد الواجب، أو ممكن فيكون محدثاً مسبوقاً بالنفي، فتكون الذوات من حيث هي مسبوقة بالنفي، وهو مع ابتنائه على كون كل ممكن الثبوت محدثاً، بمعنى المسبوق بالنفي لا ينفي كون الذوات ثابتة بدون الوجود، بل غايته أن ثبوتها في العدم مسبوق بنفيها . وأجيب بأن الواجب ما يستغني عن الغير في وجوده لا في ثبوته الذي هو أعم.
The third: if the essences (dhawat) are fixed in non-existence, and according to you their fixity is not from something else, then they would be necessary (wajiba), for the meaning of 'necessary' is nothing other than this; thus the necessity of contingent things would follow, and multiplicity of the necessary. And their elaboration: that if they are fixed, then their fixity is either necessary, resulting in multiplicity of the necessary, or possible, in which case they would be originated (muhdathan) preceded by negation; thus the essences from the aspect of themselves are preceded by negation. And this, though based on the principle that every contingent of fixity is originated, meaning preceded by negation, does not negate that the essences are fixed without existence; rather at most it indicates that their fixity in non-existence is preceded by their negation. And the answer: that the necessary (al-wajib) is what is independent of others in its existence, not in its fixity, which is more general.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This third objection argues that if non-existent essences are fixed by themselves without external cause, they would be necessary beings, leading to a plurality of necessary beings, which is impossible. The answer refines the definition of the necessary: necessity pertains to existence, not to mere fixity. Fixity (thubut) is broader and includes both the necessary and the possible. So the objection fails because it conflates fixity with existence.

Key Terms
الذوات
الثبوت
الوجوب
الواجب
الممكن
المحدث
النفي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The necessary being is what is independent in any respect, including fixity.
Correction: The necessary being is independent specifically in its existence, not in its fixity.

Checkpoint
What is the precise definition of 'necessary' according to the answer?
A) What is independent in its fixity
B) What is independent in its existence
C) What is not preceded by negation
D) What has no cause

Key Takeaway
The distinction between necessity in existence and necessity in fixity resolves the objection of multiple necessary beings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

How does this lesson's distinction between fixity and existence challenge you to see yourself not as necessary but as dependent on God's will for your actual being?
?
How often do you conflate 'being fixed' with 'being necessary' in your own thinking about God or about your own traits? Identify one self-reliant attitude in your life that you've treated as 'necessary' when it is merely 'fixed'. What would it mean to re-center that trait as dependent on God's existence?
?
The objection in this lesson leads to the absurdity of multiple necessary beings. Is there any area of your life where you functionally treat multiple things as 'necessary' (i.e., as if they must exist for your happiness)? How can the truth that necessity belongs to God alone liberate you from that false sense of necessity?
